Poonam Patil: @13135550002 what is udaygiri ratnagiri in odisha
Meta AI: Udayagiri and Ratnagiri are two famous Buddhist sites in Odisha, India. They are located in the Jajpur district, about 100 km from Bhubaneswar, the capital city of Odisha.

Udayagiri: 

- Udayagiri means "Sunrise Hill" in Sanskrit.
- It is a significant Buddhist site, with numerous monasteries, stupas, and sculptures.
- The site features a famous 1st-century BCE inscription of Emperor Kharavela, which speaks about his conquests and patronage of Buddhism.

Ratnagiri: 

- Ratnagiri means "Gem Hill" in Sanskrit.
- It is another important Buddhist site, known for its stunning sculptures, monasteries, and votive stupas.
- Ratnagiri was once a major center of Mahayana Buddhism and is believed to have been established in the 5th century CE.

Both Udayagiri and Ratnagiri are part of the "Diamond Triangle" of Odisha, along with Lalitgiri, and are renowned for their rich Buddhist heritage and architectural treasures.

Poonam Patil: *HDFC Bank may now go for the final stroke to get shareholders and RBI love.*

As per news reports, it’s selling off a part of its loan portfolio!

And it does make some sense.

..

*As a bank, HDFC Bank has always been known to maintain a very healthy credit-to-deposit ratio.*

But, post the mega-merger with housing lender HDFC Limited, that changed overnight.

The C/D ratio went from 84% or so to 115%!

And that was a big trouble.

..

*Now, of course, the bank had anticipated it, and had also told shareholders about it upfront.*

But, with time, shareholders grew impatient with this. And so did the RBI, because rising C/D ratio was an industry-wide problem.

Thus, as per news reports, RBI was informally pressuring not just HDFC Bank, but also the likes of Axis Bank to bring down their C/D ratios.

..

*Now, to do this, there are only three ways.*

1> Grow your deposit base faster than you lend

2> Slow down your lending activity deliberately, which means saying no to a lot of incoming business

3> Sell a part of your existing loan portfolio to bring down the C/D ratio

..

*So far, HDFC bank has already achieved initial success with the first two measures.*

Its C/D ratio has come down to 104% as a result.

But, its lending growth is already at a multi-quarter low now. How much more can you slow it down?

Thus, this is where the scope for the third way to address C/D ratio comes to the fore.

..

*The question now is how much of loans would it be looking to sell?*

Given how big HDFC Bank is, to bring down the C/D ratio considerably, it will have to sell a massive amount.

And there are only a handful of Indian banks or financial entities that could have the capacity and cash to buy so much.

Thus, will be very interesting to see how this plays out.

..

Aryush Tripathi: @13135550002 what's the meaning of panacea
Meta AI: A panacea is a term used to describe a solution or remedy that is considered a cure-all for a wide range of problems or diseases. It comes from the Greek myth of Panacea, the goddess of healing, who was said to have a potion that could cure any ailment.

In modern usage, a panacea is often used metaphorically to describe a solution that is perceived as a universal fix, capable of resolving multiple issues or problems simultaneously. However, it's important to note that true panaceas are rare, and most solutions have limitations and potential drawbacks.

Example: "Some people think that technology is a panacea for all our problems, but it's clear that it also has its own set of challenges and limitations."

However, it's important to acknowledge that true panaceas are rare, and most solutions have limitations, potential drawbacks, and context-dependent efficacy.

4. Set boundaries if necessary.

Poonam Patil: @13135550002 why are some people ziddi
Meta AI: The term "ziddi" is a Hindi/Urdu word that roughly translates to "stubborn" or " obstinate" in English. People can be ziddi for various reasons, including:

1. Strong convictions: Some individuals hold strong beliefs and values, making them resistant to changing their minds or opinions.
2. Fear of losing control: Certain people might feel that compromise or flexibility means losing control over a situation or decision.
3. Past experiences: Traumatic or negative experiences can shape a person's behavior, leading them to become more rigid or unyielding.
4. Personality traits: Certain personality types, like perfectionists or those with strong willpower, can be more prone to being ziddi.
5. Cultural or upbringing influences: Cultural or family backgrounds can sometimes emphasize the importance of being strong-willed or uncompromising.

It's important to note that being ziddi can be both positive (e.g., standing up for one's rights) and negative (e.g., refusing to listen to others). Understanding the underlying reasons for someone's stubbornness can help in effectively communicating and finding common ground.

Poonam Patil: Hello connections,

I am excited to share that I recently participated in a case study organized by the Consulting and Analytics Club of IIT Guwahati. The case study focused on traffic congestion in Mumbai.

Our team, consisting of Aryush Tripathi, Sumit Kumar Chaudhary, Anubhav Mishra, and myself, conducted in-depth research on the various factors contributing to congestion and proposed several potential solutions.

This project was a fantastic learning experience that enhanced my critical thinking skills as a consultant. I would like to extend my gratitude to the Consulting and Analytics Club of IIT Guwahati for hosting such a valuable event.

Feel free to check out our report through the following drive link.

Poonam Patil: Hello connections,

I am excited to share that I recently participated in a case study organized by the Consulting and Analytics Club of IIT Guwahati. The case study focused on traffic congestion in Mumbai.
Mumbai has been experiencing severe traffic congestion over the past decade. Our team—Aryush Tripathi, Sumit Kumar Chaudhary, Anubhav Mishra, and myself—conducted extensive research to systematically identify the various factors contributing to this issue using the issue tree approach. We also proposed several potential solutions.

This project was a fantastic learning experience that enhanced my critical thinking skills as a consultant. I would like to extend my gratitude to the Consulting and Analytics Club of IIT Guwahati for hosting this event.

Feel free to check out our report through the following drive link.

Poonam Patil: Hello connections,

I am excited to share that I recently participated in a case study organized by the Consulting and Analytics Club of IIT Guwahati. The case study focused on traffic congestion in Mumbai.
Mumbai has been experiencing severe traffic congestion over the past decade. Our team—Aryush Tripathi, Sumit Kumar Chaudhary, Anubhav Mishra, and myself—conducted extensive research to systematically identify the various factors contributing to this issue using the issue tree approach. We also proposed several potential solutions.

This project was a fantastic learning experience that enhanced my critical thinking skills as a consultant. I would like to extend my gratitude to the Consulting and Analytics Club of IIT Guwahati for hosting this event.

Feel free to check out our report through the following drive link.

✨ Step into Omphalos: A Journey Where Pop Culture Meets Philosophy ✨

At Omphalos, pop culture collides with philosophy, revealing mysteries within the familiar worlds of memes, movies, music, books, anime and more. Here, we let pop culture consume us, guiding us from the playful to the profound.

Join us for our first meeting to explore new perspectives, share your thoughts, and help shape the path forward. 🌌

📅 Date: Sunday, 10th November
🕕 Time: 6 PM onwards

With a strong sense of responsibility and a genuine desire to contribute to the student community, we — *Ankit Kumar Singh and Bhavya* — are delighted to announce our joint candidacy for the post of *Coordinators, Counselling Service Team (CST)* for the academic year 2025–26.

Having served as *Student Guides* and *Assistant Coordinators* in CST over the past two years, we’ve had the privilege of supporting students through their journeys — from onboarding freshers to ensuring a safe, inclusive, and welcoming environment for all.

We aspire to: 

* Ensure a smooth transition and strong support system for incoming first years

* Work actively towards improving student mental health through new initiatives and collaborations

* Expand CST’s presence and impact across the entire student body

Driven by compassion, collaboration, and commitment, we look forward to your support as we take this next step with CST.

Vote for us on *April 20th, 2025*
